Liaoning Province Pawnshops Borrow Fifty Thousand Dollars 127

Shenyang Correspondence: According to successive statements from pawnshops throughout the province to the Provincial Pawnshop Guild, the current financial stagnation and economic downturn have made life difficult for the general populace, who rely solely on pawnshops for assistance. As a result, pawnshops are receiving less money each day than they are lending out. Without sufficient reserves, they will be unable to maintain the current situation and will inevitably have to refuse to accept items for pawn or allow redemption, causing panic among the people and instability in the market. This situation is entirely due to the banks' restrictions on loans. The Guild has requested that the Liaoning Chamber of Commerce Federation contact the banking consortium to arrange for a loan of one million dollars to provide assistance. The Chamber of Commerce Federation sent a letter to the Provincial Government through the Commerce Federation, requesting that the banks be instructed to provide assistance. The Provincial Government then issued an instruction stating that the request from the Provincial Pawnshop Guild for the banking consortium to provide a loan of one million dollars to assist pawnshops had been forwarded to the Official Bank for joint discussion and response by the banks. The Official Bank has replied that it has recently extended loans to merchants in various counties, with a significant portion being borrowed by pawnshops. It is currently planning to establish more pawnshops in various counties, requiring even more capital. It is difficult to handle this loan request, but it is inappropriate to refuse entirely, given the need to maintain the market and assist the poor. After convening a meeting with the Frontier Bank, the Bank of China, and the Bank of Communications, it was agreed that it would be insufficient to provide the full amount requested. It was proposed that the four banks jointly provide 500,000 dollars in silver based on secured loan procedures. The Frontier Bank and the Official Bank would each provide 150,000 dollars, while the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications would each provide 100,000 dollars. The Bank of China and the Bank of Communications would be responsible for lending to pawnshops in the provincial capital, while the Frontier Bank would be responsible for lending to pawnshops in counties where it has branches, and the Official Bank would be responsible for the rest. It is believed that this arrangement, when combined with previous loans, would be sufficient to maintain the market, as the amount would be close to the originally requested one million dollars. The Provincial Government has approved this instruction and ordered the Chamber of Commerce Federation to notify the pawnshops. (July 30th)

Preliminary Points Regarding the Civil Code: Inheritance and Family Sections (Continued)

Review Opinions of the Central Political Council 128

(II) Community Property System: The distinguishing feature of this system is the establishment of a form of joint property for spouses, with each spouse also allowed to have separate property in addition to the joint property. The husband has the right to manage and dispose of the joint property (with several exceptions regarding the right of disposal). Upon termination of the community property relationship, both parties or their heirs may divide the joint property. Because the scope of the joint property varies, this system can be further subdivided into the following three types: A. General Community Property System (used as the statutory system in countries such as Norway, Finland, the Netherlands, and Portugal); B. Community Property System of Movables and Income (used as the statutory system in countries such as France and Belgium); C. Community Property System of Income (used as the statutory system in countries such as Soviet Russia, Spain, several South American countries, and several states in the United States). (III) Joint Property System: The wife's property, except for what is reserved, is concentrated in the husband's possession, and there is no joint property between the spouses. Instead, each spouse preserves their original property, but all is managed by the husband. The husband has the right to usufruct and, within a specific scope, the right to dispose of the property brought in by the wife. This is its distinguishing feature (used as the statutory system in countries such as Germany, Switzerland, Japan, and several states in the United States). (IV) Dowry System: Part of the wife's property is specifically designated as a dowry to provide for household expenses and is managed by the husband. This dowry is completely separate from the wife's remaining property, but the ownership still belongs to the wife (with exceptions). The husband may not transfer or mortgage all or part of the dowry (according to the survey, no country uses this as the statutory system). (V) Separate Property System: Spouses individually enjoy the rights of ownership, management, and usufruct over their own property, and household expenses are, in principle, borne equally by the spouses (used as the statutory system in countries such as Austria, the Czech Republic, Hungary, Romania, Italy, Greece, Turkey, the United Kingdom, and several states in the United States). The above-mentioned property systems for spouses are only described in broad terms. In reality, when adopting a certain system, countries often incorporate elements from other systems. For example, the joint property system stipulated in the Swiss Civil Code actually includes a community property system of income, adopting its key points as follows: 1. All property owned by both parties at the time of marriage and during the continuation of the marriage constitutes marital property, with the exception of what the wife has reserved. 2. Regarding marital property, the property belonging to the wife at the time of marriage and the property inherited or gifted to the wife during the continuation of the marriage constitutes the wife's brought-in property, and she retains ownership of it. The husband is the owner of the part of the brought-in property and marital property that does not belong to the wife. 3. The wife's earnings and the natural fruits of her brought-in property belong to the husband upon separation, with the exception of what pertains to the wife's reserved property. 4. The marital property is managed by the husband, and the management expenses are borne by the husband. The wife has the right to manage within the scope that she can represent both parties. 5. The husband has the right to usufruct the wife's brought-in property and bears the responsibilities of a usufructuary. 6. Except for management, the husband may not dispose of the wife's brought-in property without the wife's consent, except for what already belongs to the husband. 7. The wife may dispose of the marital property within the scope that she can represent both parties. Considering the above seven points, the Swiss joint property system is both convenient for maintaining a shared life and sufficient to protect the rights of both parties, striking a balance that is also suitable for our country's situation. Therefore, it is proposed to adopt it as the usual statutory system. In specific circumstances, such as one party's bankruptcy, the separate property system is naturally adopted (see Article 182 of the Swiss Civil Code). Furthermore, when one of the spouses is subject to compulsory execution of debts and cannot pay them off, the court may, at the request of the other spouse, declare the adoption of the separate property system (see Article 183 of the same law). Therefore, adopting the separate property system as the extraordinary statutory system also follows the precedents of Switzerland and other countries. It is proposed to limit the contractual systems to the following three types: (1) Community Property System; (2) Uniform Property System; (3) Separate Property System. The reason for limiting the contractual property systems to the statutory types is to avoid situations where the freedom of contract in spousal relationships lacks standards, resulting in different systems for different people, which would make transactions with third parties difficult and create a sense of distrust in society. Regarding the property system for spouses, whether it is permissible to change to another system by contract during the continuation of the marriage after it has been agreed upon is also an important related question that should be addressed. Examining various countries, some prohibit it (e.g., Belgium, Spain, Brazil, and several South American countries, France, Italy, Japan, the Netherlands, etc.), some allow it (e.g., Germany, Austria, the Czech Republic, Sweden, Denmark, etc.), and some take a compromise approach by allowing it under certain conditions (e.g., Switzerland, Turkey, Norway, the United Kingdom). It is now proposed to adopt a compromise approach, allowing both parties to enter into another contract with appropriate conditions, such as: 1. It must be permitted by the court; 2. It must not harm the rights of third parties. These conditions can provide some restrictions to avoid abuses. The number and content of the conditions should be determined when drafting the articles. Point 7: The Issue of Concubines? There is no need to stipulate anything regarding the issue of concubines. (Explanation) The system of concubinage should be abolished as soon as possible. Although it still exists in fact, the law should not recognize its existence. There is no need to specifically stipulate its status in the code or in separate laws. As for the status of their children, such as issues of inheritance and marriage restrictions, all illegitimate children are treated the same as legitimate children, and these issues have already been stipulated separately in their respective sections, so there is no need to address them separately here. Point 8: Should the Family System Be Stipulated? The family system should be stipulated in a separate chapter. (Explanation) There is still room for research on the merits and demerits of individualism versus familism today, and the Chinese family system has been the foundation of social organization for thousands of years. It may be difficult to fundamentally overturn it, or it may have too great an impact on society. In fact, it seems appropriate to preserve this type of organization. Legally, the existence of the family system should be recognized, and a separate chapter should be established to define it in detail. Point 9: The Issue of Family System Orientation (1) The provisions of the family system should be based on communal living and place more emphasis on the obligations of the family head. (2) The family head should be gender-neutral. (Explanation) The original purpose of recognizing the existence of the family system is to maintain the communal living of the entire family. Therefore, it should be based on the communal living of the family members and not on the authority of the family head. The family systems stipulated in Switzerland and the Balkan countries can serve as references. Chinese customs emphasize the rights of the family head while neglecting their obligations, and only men are qualified to be family heads while women are not, which is not in line with the current situation. Therefore, in maintaining the family system, emphasis should be placed on the obligations of the family head, and it should be clearly stipulated that the family head is gender-neutral, so that both social psychology and global trends can be taken into account. (End)

Wuhu Quick Dispatch 129

Since Wuhu decided to close the grain stabilization bureau, rice prices suddenly soared yesterday, with each dollar only buying five Sheng (originally eight Sheng). The general populace was greatly alarmed. In addition to requesting that local authorities find ways to provide relief, various groups are planning to hold a meeting tomorrow to discuss solutions.

The Municipal Education Association held a meeting today and resolved to request that the Municipal Government reorganize the Design Committee established by the Municipal Government, as it exists in name only. Furthermore, because the municipal donation collected by the Municipal Government was originally intended for local construction and education, but has recently been used entirely for the Municipal Government's expenses, which is clearly inconsistent with the original plan, it was resolved to request that the Municipal Government allocate a portion of the municipal donation for education and construction to avoid waste.

The Provincial Government, considering the bandit group that robbed the Huangmu Ferry in Nanling County a source of great danger if not completely eliminated, has telegraphed an order to Battalion Commander Feng of the 3rd Battalion stationed in Wuhu to lead his troops to suppress them. It also ordered the counties of Wuhu, Nanling, and Xuancheng to jointly suppress them. The county magistrates of the three counties have now agreed to encircle them from different directions and dispatched police teams simultaneously yesterday afternoon. They made contact with the bandits at a location twenty Li from Nanling at 2 PM today.

The Anhui Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation previously petitioned the Ministry of Finance based on a resolution of the Representative Assembly to abolish the egg tax at Fengyang Customs. The Ministry of Finance replied yesterday that it should wait until the nationwide implementation of Li tax reductions before making an overall assessment. (August 3rd)

Cooperative Instructor Arrives in Songjiang to Take Office 131

Suzhou

Closing of Taihu Lake Harbors During Bandit Suppression Period 133

Gong Guoliang, the Chief of the 3rd Water Police District, personally led a team out on July 31st to suppress bandits after being appointed as the temporary commander of bandit suppression on Taihu Lake. The bandits then fled into Zhejiang Province. While the bandits were fleeing into Zhejiang, Chen Lianzhai, the Chief of the 3rd Water Police District of Nanxun, Zhejiang, led a team toward Taihu Lake to cooperate with the Suzhou Water Police fleet in encircling and suppressing the bandits. However, the cunning bandits escaped to Yixing and Changxing. Commander Gong specially consulted with the county magistrates of Wuxian, Wujiang, and Wuxi counties and obtained their approval to close the lake harbors from tomorrow (the 6th) to the 15th, prohibiting fishing boats and civilian boats from traveling on the lake to facilitate suppression. He also telegraphed the Zhejiang Water Police team to block them during the period of harbor closure. A reward has also been offered for the capture of bandit leaders, with 100 dollars offered for each leader, 50 dollars for each "little leader," and 30 dollars for each bandit. It is also reported that Commander Gong ordered his subordinate commanders and police teams to gather in Hengjing yesterday morning (the 4th). Around 11 AM, they made contact with a bandit group at Maoqi Port and engaged in a fierce battle that lasted until 4 PM. (Details can be found in today's special report section.)

Cai Yu, the captain of the 3rd Squadron of the County Police Team, was ordered to set out to suppress bandits the day before yesterday. Fengxian Prison Warden Dismissed and Placed Under Surveillance 135

Regarding the case where fifty-eight prisoners escaped from Fengxian County Prison a few days ago, where twenty-three were shot dead by the county police team on the spot, five drowned in the river, and thirteen were captured, but seventeen still escaped, Chief Judge Lin of the High Court sent Yao Guozhang, the Director of the Prison Department, to investigate, and he has now returned to the court and submitted a report. After reviewing the report, Chief Judge Lin obtained the approval of the Ministry of Justice to first dismiss the prison warden of the county, Liu Ou, and place him under surveillance, transferring him to Suzhou and handing him over to the High Procuratorate for investigation to determine whether there was any suspicion of favoritism. The vacancy in the county will be temporarily filled by Miao Wenzhu, the prison warden of Jinshan County. The vacancy in Jinshan County will be filled by Cheng Futang, the warden of the Jiangdu County Court Detention Center.

Wuxi

Two Robberies Occurred Overnight 136

In our county, robberies in the countryside have been occurring one after another, causing deep concern about the future of public safety. Yesterday at 2:30 AM, a group of over ten robbers suddenly appeared at the home of Jin Deqing, a needlepoint doctor in the twelfth and thirteenth districts (Wan'an City) of Sun Lane. They wore masks, short clothes, and carried knives and clubs. Unable to enter because the main gate was tightly closed, they knocked on the door, pretending to call for a doctor. Jin Deqing, startled from his sleep, believed them and opened the door. The robbers rushed into the house, went straight to the bedroom, dragged Jin Kui (the current township chief) off the bed, and forced him to hand over silver dollars. They then stabbed Jin Kui in the chest with a sharp knife, causing him to bleed profusely and fall to the ground in pain. The robbers then ransacked the house, stealing 120 silver dollars and all the land deeds. As they left, they said that Yang Peicheng (from Fengzhuang) should bring 3,000 dollars to redeem the land deeds. The victim has reported the incident to the county authorities and requested an investigation. Also, yesterday morning, a group of over ten robbers, each carrying a handgun and a flashlight, climbed over the trees into the home of Ding Yaoliang, a resident of the Shang area of the Zhizhang River near Luoshe in the fourteenth and fifteenth districts. They ransacked the house for half an hour before leaving and robbing the neighboring home of Ding Yuqing, taking gold jewelry, clothing, and cash worth about 300 dollars.

Party Headquarters Reports Use of Obsolete Seals 141

The County Executive Committee has received a report from the first branch of the second district stating that a judicial police officer, Xu Yongping, claimed to be searching for opium at the home of Zhu Aisheng in Nantai Riben Bridge. However, the search warrant was issued in the name of the County Public Office, not the County Government, and the seal was an obsolete Fengxian County seal, not the current Fengxian County Government seal. It was determined to be a forgery and should be photographed and reported for investigation. At the same time, the County Government reported that the police officer seized opium at Zhu's house and wanted to take it back, but it was intercepted and the summons was destroyed. The Party and Government are now giving different accounts and have sent special investigators to investigate.

Reform Measures for Land Tax Collection 142

The Finance Bureau believed that there were many abuses in the collection of busy canal surcharges, so it requested the County Government to formulate new measures for reform. It has now been decided to implement the new system from the busy season of the 19th year. The Finance Bureau will print three-part forms and distribute them to the land tax collection offices in advance. The tu zheng will complete the forms at the counter when paying the grain tax. The collection office will fill in the amount payable, give one copy to the bureau, keep one copy in the counter, and give one copy to the tu zheng for safekeeping. The tu zheng will then personally take the payment and the form to the cashier. The collection office is only responsible for calculating and filling out the forms and is not allowed to collect money directly.

Conspiracy to Kidnap Wealthy Households: No Definite Confession 148

Li Hongze, an inspector of the Public Security Bureau, was accused by the County Party Headquarters of conspiring with bandits to kidnap wealthy households in Changshou. The Public Security Bureau detained Li Hongze, Xu Yongliang, and others. Yesterday morning, Director Li conducted a preliminary interrogation. Xu Yongliang, 23, who lived in the west gate and was a primary school teacher, stated that the pistol was found near Xu Yun, but he did not know where it came from. Li Rongbao lived next door to him, and Xu Yun stayed at a hotel for several days, with Li Hongze paying for the room. Later, he borrowed a dollar from him. After leaving the hotel, Xu Yun stayed at his house for several days. He did not know that Xu Yun borrowed a gun from Li Hongze. Xu Yun, 20, from Zhouzhuang, stated that he was a second-year student at Yancheng Middle School in Suzhou and had a teacher-student relationship with Li Hongze. He borrowed the gun from him for self-defense and had no other intentions. Li Rongbao, 30, who lived in the west gate and worked for a transport company, stated that he did not know Li Hongze and Xu Yun until Xu Yongliang introduced them. Xu Yongliang was his neighbor. On the day the pistol was found, he was next door when it was found under Xu Yun's bed. Li Hongze was also there. He had left the transport company four or five years ago and had been in the 17th Army for three or four years. He did not know that they had borrowed the gun. Li Hongze, 20, a merchant from Changshou, stated that he did not lend the pistol to Xu Yongliang, but forgot it in Xu Yun's room, No. 17 of the Zhaoshang Hotel, on the afternoon of July 30th at 6:00 PM. Xu Yun had stayed there for several days without paying the bill, so he paid it because of their teacher-student relationship. Xu Yun asked to borrow money from him, but he did not give it to him. He then went back, even taking the pistol. He did not know Li Rongshi at all. When he went to get the pistol, Xu Yun was still sleeping and he grabbed him. The gun was taken from under the bed. After the interrogation, they will be sent to the County Government for handling today (the 4th).

(Presenting) to the government for record (1) Presenting to the government for an order to its subordinates to effectively protect and encourage the beekeeping industry (1) Presenting to the government for a clear order to exempt all kinds of donations and taxes for bee species, honey, wax, etc. (1) Requesting the government to effectively resist the import of Japanese bees in order to avoid the spread of bee diseases.

Temporary Martial Law in Wuqing Town 150

On the 31st of last month, Wuqing Town, which is located at the intersection of Wu Xing and Tong Xiang counties, received a phone call saying that a large group of hundreds of bandits in more than 30 boats were sailing from Jiangsu Province to Zhejiang. After confirming the information, the town was under temporary martial law by Wang the leader of the water police, Cui the leader of the security team, and the directors of the public security bureaus and Wang the leader of the anti-smuggling team of the two towns. The streets were heavily guarded by soldiers and police to check pedestrians. Tea houses, hotels, and restaurants were carefully inspected. The lights were on all night. Zhejiang-Fujian Highway Passes Through Shaoxing and Xiaoshan 152

The construction cost for earthwork, crossbeams, culverts, and mountain opening is now uniformly calculated at 600 yuan per kilometer, totaling 2,346,000 yuan. The measuring is about 480 kilometers long and is planned to be measured in three sections: from Shaoxing to Shengxian, from Xinchang to Huangyan, and from Yueqing to Pingyang. The budget for the measurement has been approved by the Construction Department, totaling 41,847 yuan.

Shaoxing

County Chamber of Commerce States Unemployment Relief Case 153

After the County Chamber of Commerce investigated the social and economic situation yesterday, it presented relief measures to the county government. In the industrial and commercial aspects, there are no large-scale industries to speak of other than the foil, wine, and silk industries. The foil industry in Shaoxing involves no less than 300,000 people, including manufacturers and vendors. Although the annual tax revenue of this product reaches 1,670,000 yuan, due to the continuous improvement of social culture and knowledge on the one hand and the weakening of the economic ability of the people on the other hand, there is a gradual concept of abolishing tin foil. Therefore, in the past one or two years, foil shops and foil shops have closed down one after another due to poor business conditions, and there are many workers who are unemployed in the foil industry. The relief methods should be divided into two types: fundamental cure and palliative cure. The fundamental cure should be to establish vocational schools to provide young people in the foil industry with relevant vocational education so that they can make a living in the future and avoid the tragedy of unemployment. The palliative cure should be to jointly establish large-scale factories by the government and local authorities to enable all the workers in the foil industry to work in factories to replace the labor force. This is a fundamental transformation for the foil industry. Shaoxing wine is a major product of Shaoxing, with an annual tax revenue of about one million yuan. However, its raw materials are mostly purchased from other provinces, which is very different from products made entirely from local raw materials. Therefore, those engaged in this industry are no different from using labor to exchange for wages. The heavy donations and taxes increase the burden, and the chaos of war and bandits obstruct transportation, all of which are enough to suppress the development of the wine industry. The relief methods should be to reduce tax rates and eliminate chaos to facilitate transportation and alleviate business difficulties. This is a fundamental maintenance for the wine industry. Yue silk is also a major product of Shaoxing. In recent years, imported clothing materials have flooded the market, causing domestic silk to be unsalable and profit rights to be lost. Fangqiao and Huahe in Shaoxing were originally known for producing silk. Now, due to the failure of the silk industry, the silk shops have closed down, the machine workers have stopped weaving, and no less than tens of thousands of workers are unemployed. And the relief methods, on the one hand, should actively promote domestic products so that the sales of domestic silk can be expanded to replace imported clothing materials.

The Shanghai Children's Army's Trip to Japan 156

Arriving in Shanghai around August 3rd

(Kobe Express News) After it was reported that a group of 42 members of the Shanghai University Children's Army, led by Ni Jiaxi, traveled to Japan, they visited famous scenic spots such as Osaka, Nara, and Kyoto, and visited urban cultural facilities. On July 15, they arrived in Yokohama and were received by Liu Zhang, the head of the local Chinese Children's Army in Japan, and executives of the Japan Boy Scout Federation. They stayed at the Chinese Association and attended a welcome tea party. On the 16th, they went to Enoshima and Kamakura to enjoy the beautiful scenery and swim in the sea. On the 17th, they had a friendly match with the Chinese basketball team. The next morning, they took a tram to Tokyo and received a warm welcome. The modern civilization of the Japanese capital after its reconstruction, the orderliness of traffic, the prosperity of department stores, the abundance of parks, and the popularity of sports all surprised and impressed the group. After staying for two days, they took a train from Ueno to Nikko to visit historical sites and famous scenic spots, and camped out in tents. Unfortunately, the continuous rain reduced their interest. Subsequently, they were invited by Count Mishima, the president of the Japan Boy Scout Federation, to stay at his villa in Shiobara Nasu for three nights. Count Mishima is the Japanese representative of the International Boy Scout Federation. This time, he provided cordial hospitality and was very amiable. After July 27, they arrived in Yokohama. That night, they held a bonfire game with the Chinese and Japanese Boy Scouts. About 300 people attended. The gathering of young people from the two countries was a truly unprecedented international event for the local Boy Scouts. On the 28th, they bid farewell on the Haruna Maru and headed to Kobe. On the 30th, when the ship docked, due to a misreport by the shipping company, the local Chinese Boy Scouts were unable to arrive. Only Mr. Zeng Yanhua, a compatriot, welcomed them alone. Later, Mr. Udaka, a member of the Kobe Japanese Boy Scout Committee, and Mr. Omori, a Kobe city secretary, arrived on the ship. Mr. Zeng introduced them and provided translation services. They were impressed by the special preferential treatment provided by the Japanese authorities, who provided free tram rides to Tenjin Beach. That night, Hyogo Prefecture and Kobe City jointly hosted the Shanghai University Children's Army at the Central Pavilion Western Restaurant. Representatives of the Japanese authorities delivered speeches to welcome them and expressed their hope that the young nationals of China and Japan would be able to contact each other frequently in the future to foster friendship and benefit the diplomatic relations between the two countries. Then, Team Leader Ni stood up to thank them and praised the progress of Japanese culture and the warm hospitality received from all parties during this trip, expressing his deep gratitude. After the banquet, the team members acted freely and returned to the ship around 10:00 PM for one night. As for tomorrow (July 31), they will visit the Kawasaki Shipyard at 8:00 AM. It is said that this procedure was arranged by the authorities and the Ministry of the Navy with special approval, which shows the thoughtfulness of the Japanese side's hospitality. At 11:00 AM, they will have a friendly match with the overseas Chinese Tongwen Junior High School basketball team (results will be reported later). They are scheduled to depart from Kobe at 3:00 PM to return to Shanghai. According to a report on July 11, the team has been traveling around for two weeks. The team members are all energetic and healthy. This trip is the happiest one they have had. (Sent on July 30)

The Municipal Education Bureau Orders Schools Not to Elect "Queens"

The Municipal Education Bureau issued an order yesterday to all levels of schools in the city, stating: "The Shanghai First District Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party (Kuomintang) has sent an official letter stating that the title of 'Queen' is a form of honorific title from the imperial era. Now that the form of government has changed, how can such feudalistic titles be allowed to continue? The election of 'Queens' has become fashionable in various schools, with each school imitating the other, which is no different from preserving the influence of general feudal ideas. We request that you be consulted to ban this practice and instruct all newspapers to avoid using the term 'Queen' when publishing photos of female students." The bureau believes that the points raised in the letter are well-founded and should be verified and handled. The bureau believes that the title of "Queen" belongs to the imperial era, and now that the form of government has long been changed, it is no longer appropriate to use this title, which contains feudal ideas. Hereafter, schools must not hold any more "Queen" elections, and the title "Queen" must not be used. In addition to instructing all newspapers to avoid using the term "Queen" when publishing photos of female students, all levels of schools are hereby ordered to comply with this order.

Shanghai Bank Establishes School Consultation Service

Shanghai is home to a large number of schools, making it the educational hub of the country. Students seeking education need to know the differences between the schools' curricula, tuition fees, and locations. The Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank is dedicated to serving the community and believes that supporting and promoting education is its responsibility. In addition to establishing offices at many schools in Shanghai and collecting tuition fees on behalf of schools, the bank has now established a school consultation department at its headquarters and branches in the city to assist students. The department provides enrollment brochures for universities and middle schools in Shanghai and across the country. If you have other questions, you can also consult or contact the bank. It is said that this service has been well received by the academic community.

China Women's Physical Education School Holds Alumni Meeting Yesterday

The China Women's Physical Education School on Qingyun Road, Zhabei, held its annual alumni meeting yesterday. Graduates from previous classes attended. Ji Guozhen was elected as chairman, and Zhou Jicheng as secretary. Principal Hua reported on the school's situation and the development of school affairs over the years. Japanese Soccer Team Embarks on Overseas Expedition

The team will depart on the 17th of this month and return on October 14th, aiming for a decisive battle against the Chinese team four years later. Japanese soccer has traditionally been underdeveloped, consistently ranking last in the Far East Games, which has been a source of shame for the Japanese sports community. To rectify this, Japan has spared no effort in soccer training over the past three years, employing various scientific research methods to improve their skills. Players have also been given financial support. As a result, the progress of Japanese soccer has been remarkable. At the 8th Shanghai Games, they surprisingly won second place, a groundbreaking achievement. Not content with this, Japan has been diligently promoting soccer at home for the past two years, resulting in a significant increase in strength. At the recent Tokyo Games, they tied with China for first place, with the championship being held over until the next Games. Japan considers this four-year period an excellent opportunity to train their players' skills. Therefore, they have initiated an expedition to the United States to learn from others' strengths and compensate for their own weaknesses, with the aim of competing against the Chinese team in a decisive battle at the 10th Far East Games four years later and capturing the championship. What is most astonishing is that the players are not constrained by economic concerns and are all full-time professionals without occupational distractions. It is doubtful that our country can compare to this situation. Japan, aware that the Chinese team has already begun its expedition to Europe, has decided that its team will depart for the Americas and Canada on August 17th. All preparations for the expedition have been completed. Prior to departure, they will conduct two weeks of intensive training at the foot of Mount Fuji, with two intense matches every morning and evening. The leader and coach of the expedition are Mr. Kameyama and Mr. Hobimi. The itinerary is as follows:

August 1st to 14th: Training camp

August 17th: Depart from Yokohama in the afternoon

August 29th: Arrive in Vancouver, Canada

September 1st: First match against Vancouver team

September 6th: Second match against Vancouver team

September 13th: First match against Victoria

September 17th: Second match against Victoria

September 24th: Match against Columbia team

September 27th: Match against Columbia University

September 28th: Visit Seattle

September 29th: Return to Vancouver

October 14th: Return to Yokohama

Shanghai International Tennis Tournament to Be Held on August 13th

The Shanghai Tennis Tournament originally had the International Robert Cup as the focus of international competition each year, but only one doubles match could not generate enough interest. This season, the Chinese Tennis Association initiated the Shanghai International Tennis Championship, with Rotary President Fuliqi donating a valuable trophy to be held annually, similar to the Davis Cup. The competition method is also based on the Davis Cup system, with four singles groups and one doubles group, which is a groundbreaking innovation in the tennis world. It is expected that the United States, Britain, Portugal, Japan, France, and Germany will join. The Chinese Tennis Association held a committee meeting yesterday and decided that the competition will be held on August 13th. The results of the meeting are summarized below:

The Chinese Tennis Association Committee held a meeting at the Western Restaurant of the YMCA on Sichuan Road yesterday afternoon. Local News

Songhu Garrison Headquarters

Notice to Maintain Public Order

Punishment Under Military Law for Those Who Disrupt Local Order and Traffic

Garrison Headquarters Notice on the Songhu Garrison Area: This notice concerns the fact that we are currently in a time of war, and the security of the rear areas is extremely important. Songhu is a crucial location with a mix of Chinese and foreign residents. Enemy agents often take advantage of communists and bandits to incite unrest and create disturbances, attempting to commit wrongdoing. The Headquarters, for the safety of the people of Songhu and to maintain local order, must strictly guard against and suppress any signs of unrest. Therefore, we issue this notice to inform everyone that anyone who, without authorization, gathers a crowd to disrupt local order, regardless of their identity, will be punished under military law for disturbing the rear areas. There will be no leniency. Anyone who reports such activities in advance, leading to the cracking of a case, will be rewarded generously. We urge everyone to be vigilant. Commander Xiong Shihui

Preventing Disruption of Traffic

Headquarters Notice to Both Road Bureaus: This notice concerns the fact that we are currently in a time of war, and the traffic on the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou Railways is crucial. We fear that unscrupulous individuals may be lurking, plotting to disrupt traffic. The Headquarters, to maintain the safety of both roads and local order, has already ordered military police along the lines to conduct strict inspections. Therefore, we issue this notice to inform everyone that residents in the vicinity must not harbor bandits, disrupt traffic, or engage in any activities that may hinder the operation of the railways. Otherwise, once discovered, anyone, regardless of their identity, will be punished under military law for disturbing the rear areas. There will be no leniency. Anyone who reports such activities in advance, leading to the cracking of a case, will be rewarded generously. We urge everyone to be vigilant.

Postal Service Dispute Resolved

Satisfactory Results from Yesterday's Two Rounds of Negotiations

Postal Workers to Receive an Additional Two Yuan Rice Subsidy Per Month

The ten unresolved issues between the Shanghai Postal Workers Union and the Employees Union, which had been delayed for nearly a year, were finally resolved. On the 24th of last month, a general request was submitted to the Post Office General Administration, requesting a satisfactory response within five days. Wei Yifu, Director-General of the Post Office General Administration, repeatedly sent his secretary, Mr. Yang Sili, to negotiate with representatives of the two unions, but without success. The two sides nearly reached a breaking point. Fearing that this would lead to unrest, Director-General Wei personally came to Shanghai the day before yesterday to discuss the matter with Wang Boqun, Minister of Communications. He then prepared to resolve the postal workers' strike peacefully. Yesterday, he convened representatives of the two unions for two rounds of negotiations. As a result of mutual concessions, the impending strike was averted. The details are as follows:

Negotiation Details

Wei Yifu, Director-General of the Post Office, concurrently serves as Vice Minister of the Ministry of Communications. Recently, the assassination of Zhao Tieqiao, Director-General of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, has caused him much concern. Furthermore, Minister Wang Boqun suffered a slight illness during his tenure in Shanghai last week, delaying his return to Beijing until the night before last. Director-General Wei, burdened by ministerial affairs, was unable to leave Beijing until the day before yesterday and arrived in Shanghai. Upon arriving in Shanghai, he immediately intended to convene representatives of the unions to discuss ways to approach the situation. However, as that day was a Sunday, he was unable to contact the union representatives. Yesterday morning, he finally sent the notice to hold negotiations to the union representatives, inviting two representatives from each union to the Director-General's office at 9 AM yesterday morning. The representatives of the Postal Employees Union, Fu Dewei, Tang Yong, Wang Yuguang, and Zhu Hailan, and the representatives of the Postal Workers Union, Zhu Xuefan, Lu Jingshi, Zhang Kechang, and Qi Jiamou, arrived at the Director-General's office at 10 AM to begin formal negotiations. After three hours, most of the ten conditions had been agreed upon, and it was agreed to continue negotiations at 4 PM. At 4:30 PM, the two sides resumed negotiations at the same location. Finally, through mutual concessions, the remaining issues were resolved satisfactorily.

Resolved Conditions

The conditions resolved through negotiations between the two sides yesterday are as follows: (A) Regarding (1) the timely publication of the postal service's economic final accounts and budgets in each district; (2) the issue of the Director-General's secretary not being entitled to the same treatment as postal personnel, and the correction of Bureau Order No. 208; (3) the issue of preferential examinations for letter carriers and messengers who have served for more than 15 years to be promoted to postal assistants; (4) the establishment of a new grade of messenger within the bureau to accommodate letter carriers who are injured in the line of duty or elderly; (5) the restoration of the national personnel transfer semi-monthly publication: all five items will be implemented in accordance with the union's requested opinions. (B) All postal personnel nationwide will receive a subsidy of two yuan per month due to the low value of silver. (C) Year-end bonuses: those who have served for more than one year but less than ten years will receive one-fourth of a month's salary; those who have served for more than ten years will receive one and a half months' salary. (D) Improve the treatment of child messengers: (1) The title of "child messenger" will be changed; (2) the starting salary will be changed to 15 yuan, and the highest salary will be changed to 21 yuan; (3) those who cannot pass the examination to become postal assistants after three years will be reassigned as messengers; (4) other benefits, such as holidays, annual bonuses, and death benefits, will be the same. (E) The issue of revising the salaries of all grades below postal assistant will be resolved by representatives of the union in consultation with the authorities within two months and implemented from July 1st. (F) The issue of improving holidays will be improved by representatives of the two unions in consultation with the authorities within one month. After the Director-General made these decisions, the representatives of the two unions were satisfied and convened a general meeting of the members of each department and team that night to report on the progress. At that time, it was decided to hold a dinner party on Sunday of this week for those who participated in this work. Regarding the issue of opposing Liu Shufan and merging the remittance and savings bureau with the post office, it is reported that the union will send representatives to Beijing to petition separately.

Port Authority Rushes to Repair the East Embankment Seawall

Since the sudden hurricane on July 14th and 15th, the sea surface has been surging with tides. All the original seawall surfaces at Dongtang, the 20 zhang and 34 zhang sections at the north end of the "Ai" character series, the 45 zhang section at the east end of the Shenjiazhai "Shou" character series, the 6 zhang 5 chi and 10 zhang sections at the end of the work, the 15 zhang section at the north end of the Daijiazhai "Shuai" character series, and the 38 zhang section of the "Yizhou" character series of the Yizhou Embankment have been washed away, with soil losses of three, four, or five chi. The situation is extremely critical. Fortunately, the Port Authority Seawall Office immediately discovered the situation and reported it to the Port Authority, requesting funds to purchase materials and transport them to the construction site. The most important parts were urgently blocked. On the 27th, 28th, and 29th, another hurricane struck, howling wildly at night, accompanied by torrential rain. The storm surge in Dongtang directly impacted the seawall, with the tide level only three chi away from the top of the seawall. The situation was extremely dangerous and unprecedented in recent years. Among them, the "Jiang" character series, which is located at the intersection of the Yangtze River and the ocean's storm surge, and the "Shuai" character series, which has a more protruding seawall and the narrowest bund and is the most vulnerable to the sea tide, had sections that were repaired last year. For example, the three sections at the north end of the Biao family's residence in the "Jiang" character series, totaling 67 zhang in length, and one section at the east end of the Dai family's residence in the "Shuai" character series, totaling 5 zhang in length, all the built-up earthen seawalls were washed away, the stone slopes were cracked, and the situation was on the verge of collapse. The soil-filled sacks were also scattered and disappeared. In addition to the above-mentioned 5 zhang, another 11 zhang were destroyed in the "Shuai" character series section, totaling 16 zhang. In the "Rong" character series section, only 10 zhang were washed away, with the seawall surface being 8-9 chi to over a zhang. The Port Authority is requesting funds to purchase materials and urgently carry out repairs.

Dazhong Steamer Sinks After Hitting Reef

Crew and Sailors All Rescued

Losses Exceed 200,000 Yuan

The Dazhong steamer, owned by the Shanghai Heng'an Shipping Company, specializes in routes to various ports in the South China Sea, carrying only passengers and cargo, not passengers. Last month, it carried a large shipment of Rangoon rice to eastern Zhejiang. In late last month, it loaded a large shipment of goods in Shanghai and sailed to Fujian. When the ship reached the waters off Fuzhou, it encountered a strong wind. The ship was hit by waves and struck a reef in the waters off Fuzhou. The bottom of the ship was first pierced by a submerged reef, and seawater rushed into the cargo hold. The water level in each hold rose further, and the ship began to sink into the sea. After the accident, the shipowner urgently sent a distress signal. A strong storm arose on the sea, and the Dazhong steamer was driven by the storm waves into a cluster of reefs, causing the hull to be breached in more than one place. Seeing no hope of rescue, the crew and sailors took life jackets, sampans, and other life-saving equipment to escape. It was later learned that a passing ship sent a telegram to Fuzhou to report the incident and assist in the rescue, allowing all crew members on the Dazhong steamer, from the shipowner to the sailors, to be rescued without injury. However, the Dazhong steamer was completely destroyed. All the cargo and the crew's luggage were lost at sea. The total loss is estimated to be at least 200,000 yuan. The ship, with a displacement of over 2,000 tons, had peace insurance in Shanghai. After the accident, Heng'an Company notified the passengers and insurance companies to send personnel to the site of the accident for inspection.

Chongsha Shipping Industry Competition Mediation Breaks Down

Last year, the six shipping companies on the Shanghai-Taiwan route suffered significant losses due to excessive competition. After mediation by the Ministry of Communications and the Shanghai Shipping Association, the six companies formed a joint company alliance. Business has improved significantly in the past six months. Unexpectedly, one wave has just subsided, and another has risen. Six shipping companies on the Chongsha line suddenly started competing for business. To protect the interests of fellow businesses, the Shanghai Shipping Association intervened to mediate. Unexpectedly, yesterday's mediation meeting broke down. This matter is of great importance to the coastal shipping industry. The situation is described below:

Truth About the Competition

There are six companies operating ships on the Shanghai-Haimen Chongsha route, including Ping'an, Jufeng, Daxing, Dada, Baofeng, and Xinxinglong. One month ago, Ping'an Company first lowered prices to compete, reducing the original fare of six dimes per person from Shanghai to Chongsha to 300 wen, a decrease of nearly seven or eight tenths. The other five shipping companies had no choice but to reduce prices as well. Ping'an then suspended the Baohua ship for major repairs. The five companies have suffered significant losses in the past month or so.

Reasons for Mediation

Recently, Ping'an Company's old Baohua ship has been repaired and will soon resume service. The company's manager, Chen Shutang, sent a letter to the Shanghai Shipping Association, requesting that the committee members of the association intervene and mediate with the other five companies, such as Dada, to restore the original price. The Shanghai Shipping Association received the letter and believed that the matter concerned fellow businesses and should intervene to mediate. The association publicly appointed Liu Shisun, Yuan Ludeng, Chen Ganqing, and others as arbitration committee members, advising the six companies to abandon the mutually destructive competition and quickly cooperate, following the precedent of the Shanghai-Taiwan line. Yesterday, the representatives of the six companies were invited to the meeting to discuss the solution.

Breakdown of the Situation

Yesterday afternoon, Chen Shutang of Ping'an, Xu Zhongxin of Daxing, and Shen Qinqin of Jufeng arrived at the Shipping Association. The mediation committee members, Liu, Yuan, and Chen, explained that there should be a spirit of cooperation on the same route and that business has improved since the six companies on the Shanghai-Taiwan route formed a joint venture, which is clear evidence. They then discussed the mediation plan, which was also based on the precedent of the Shanghai-Taiwan line, estimating the total annual revenue of the Chongsha route at 600,000 yuan and allocating it among the six companies according to the size of their ships. The ship with the most seats would be allocated 115,000 yuan per year, and the ship with the fewest seats would be allocated 95,000 yuan. After the agreement was reached, Chen Shutang of Ping'an suddenly requested that the Baohua ship be counted as a first-class ship, which was opposed by the five companies because the Baohua ship had fewer seats than the other five ships. The two sides refused to back down, resulting in the invalidation of the resolution. The mediation committee members were also angered and disregarded the situation, leading to the dissolution of the meeting. The Chongsha shipping companies are still disrupting each other in competition.

Pujiang Commercial Steamer Causes Accident, Ikoma Maru Damaged

The Ikoma Maru, a Japanese-Chinese class steamer of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company, was unloading cargo at the post office dock in Shanghai after arriving from Kobe. When a certain French steamer was leaving the port and turning east outside the Waibaidu Bridge, the current was swift, and the ship was pushed by the tide. It was unable to stop and collided with the bow and outer side of the Ikoma Maru steamer. The hull of the Ikoma Maru was breached immediately. Fortunately, the damage was above the waterline and did not affect the cargo in the cabin. After learning of the incident, the Japanese Mail Steamship Company sent personnel to verify the damage. Repairs began yesterday.

Daji Maru Injured

The Daji Maru, a Yangtze River steamer of the Nissin Steamship Company, was docked at the Hongkou headquarters pier on the right side of the Japanese Mail Steamship Company dock, forming a head-to-tail connection with the Ikoma Maru. When the Ikoma Maru was hit, the impact was so great that the hull of the Daji Maru was hit by the Ikoma Maru, and its right outer side was also damaged. Personnel were sent to inspect the damage yesterday.

The Vocational Education Society Strives to Improve the Countryside 163

Planning to Establish a Rural Improvement Training Institute

The Chinese Vocational Education Society is making considerable efforts to improve the countryside. Recently, as more places are managing rural improvements, the society is entrusted to hire talent for this task. However, there are often insufficient people to meet the demand. Therefore, a Rural Improvement Training Institute has been established to recruit ten fellows and provide them with appropriate training, with the aim of turning them into capable personnel who can practically engage in rural improvement work. Experts have now been hired to preside over the institute, and official approval has been obtained for record-keeping. Recruitment has already begun. Those who are interested should send a letter before the 20th of this month, detailing their experiences and aspirations, directly to the society at the intersection of Hualong Road and Huanlong Road in the French Concession of Shanghai. The society will then arrange an interview. The institute's brief outline is listed below:

Article 1: This institute aims to improve rural affairs, based on the principle of integrating wealth and education, in order to cultivate practical working talent.

Article 2: This institute is established by the Chinese Vocational Education Society and is therefore named the Chinese Vocational Education Society Rural Improvement Training Institute.

Article 3: This institute has one director appointed by the society, one assistant, and several instructors appointed by the director.

Article 4: This institute recruits ten fellows with the following qualifications: (1) Graduation from a normal school or higher secondary school; (2) Clear understanding of literature and science; (3) Fluent language skills; (4) Strong physical health; (5) Simplicity and endurance; (6) Interest in rural life; (7) Age above twenty.

Article 5: A summary of the training subjects is as follows: (1) Village governance; (2) Economy; (3) Education; (4) Agriculture; (5) Natural sciences; (6) Other subjects will be added as needed, depending on the locality and the needs of the fellows.

Article 6: The training period is standardized according to the academic ability of the fellows, ranging from one to two years. Upon successful completion of the examination, the society will issue a certificate and assign or recommend them to appropriate places to serve.

Article 7: Fellows are exempt from tuition and accommodation fees and pay a monthly food fee of six yuan and miscellaneous fees of one yuan.

Article 8: The first address of this institute is Xu Gong Bridge in Kunshan County, Jiangsu Province, and the second address is Huang Xu Town in Zhenjiang County.

Article 9: The starting date of this institute is set for September 6th, 1920 (the recruitment and examination period will be announced separately).

Article 10: The institute's operational procedures and academic rules will be stipulated in separate regulations.

County Bureau of Education Bureau Meeting 164

The Shanghai County Bureau of Education held its 160th weekly memorial service and bureau meeting yesterday morning. Attendees included Supervisor Zhu, Zheng Guozhai, Sun Tingfang, Lin Weiwen, Niu Zhiyi, Yao Juechen, Yan Chongguang, Xi Sibu, Cai Xingsan, Wu Renda, and Pan Sansheng. Supervisor Zhu chaired the meeting, and Pan Sansheng took the minutes. After observing the formalities, the report on matters was brief, followed by the discussion of the following items:

(1) Regarding how to designate personnel for the continued operation of the joint office for volunteer education to conduct correspondence training for teachers, it was resolved to designate Wu Pengfei and twelve others to report before August 20th.

(2) Regarding the recommendation of members to review the housing repair fees for the civil education experimental area, it was resolved to recommend Zheng Guozhai, Sun Tingfang, and Xi Sibu to review the fees.

(3) Regarding the request from the Beiqiao Center Tea Garden to allocate subsidies for July, it was resolved to allocate the funds as requested.

(4) Regarding how to collect and submit various regulations for social education undertakings to the provincial department, it was resolved to collect and compile materials from all social education institutions under the bureau's jurisdiction, in addition to those already held by the bureau.

(5) Regarding the request from Yongwan Elementary School to allocate temporary expenses, it was resolved that the budget for the year had already been established and should be strictly adhered to in accordance with the provincial order. The temporary expenses requested by the school should be handled in accordance with the budget standards.

(6) Regarding the letter from Chief Wang of the Sixth District urging the recovery of the deposit from Qixin Pawnshop, it was resolved to inform the debtor and request a prompt response regarding the handling of the matter in order to bring it to a conclusion. The meeting then adjourned.
