Strict Ban on Bathing in the Huangpu River 166

As summer arrives and the weather is hot, groups of children are often seen learning to swim in the Huangpu River on both the east and west banks. However, those unfamiliar with swimming often lose their footing and drown, which has been frequently reported. Zhang Mingqin, the district chief of the Third District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, has issued a public notice at various docks in view of this situation:

"It has been learned from the report of Wang Luozhang, the patrol officer of the Huatong Warehouse, on the 2nd of this month that a boy's body was found floating in the Huangpu River at 9:00 a.m. Upon investigation, it was found to be the son of Yang Xisheng, named Shunfa, aged twelve, who drowned while bathing at the Garden Stone Bridge. In light of this, it is noted that water and fire are inherently merciless. The tides of the river are even more dangerous. How can children know the risk of losing their lives? Those who speak only sigh, and those who hear are filled with pity. Hereafter, those who bathe in the river along the banks will be considered to be acting carelessly. Adult men will be taken to the district for punishment, and the parents or elder brothers of young children will be held responsible. The police officers at each post are responsible for maintaining the health of the people and should earnestly investigate and prohibit such activities. Do not treat this as a mere formality. All must strictly abide by this notice without fail."

Trial Opens in Case of Russian Shooting Portuguese Man 167

Russian Denies Shooting

Witnesses to Be Summoned for Further Questioning

Mr. Lao Lai Luo, a Portuguese man currently employed at the Jianghai Customs, residing at No. 191 Haig Road in the French Concession, was returning to his residence by car at 9:30 p.m. on the 1st of this month after finishing his work. He was accompanied by an English woman, Miss Lao Ying. As they drove near the Hongqiao Road airfield in western Shanghai, a car in front of them stopped on the side of the road. A Russian man inside the car raised his hand and asked Mr. Lao's car to stop temporarily, and he asked to borrow a tire pump. Mr. Lao replied that he did not have such an item. Unexpectedly, the Russian man became angry and suddenly took out a pistol from his side and shot at Mr. Lao. A loud bang was heard, and the bullet entered the front of his chest, piercing his clothes. Fortunately, he was not injured, which was due to the rustiness of the pistol and its weak projectile force. Otherwise, it would have certainly resulted in bloodshed. After the Russian man fired the shot, he drove away quickly. Mr. Lao also returned home by car and reported the incident to the French police that night. The next day, Chinese and Western newspapers reported on the incident. The head of the Jing'an Temple police station, upon reading the reports, determined that the shooting location was within the jurisdiction of the police station and specially dispatched Western Detective Mike Wylen to the French police station to investigate the matter the day before. He then learned that the Russian man who fired the shot was Chai Wanlin, residing at No. 532 Xiafei Road. He went to arrest Chai and searched his residence, finding 107 bullets. He also brought Chai's driver, a Russian named Yishanke, to the French police station for questioning about the whereabouts of the pistol. Chai claimed that he had discarded the gun after firing it. The Western detective then took Mr. Chai to the place where he had discarded the weapon and subsequently found the original pistol. Yesterday morning, Chai and others were sent to the Special District Court, where Judge Wu presided over the trial. The police lawyer, Li Zhishan, presented the case and stated that the plaintiff, the Portuguese man, and the English woman who was in the car had not yet arrived in court. He requested that the relevant consuls be notified to order their presence at the next hearing. Western Detective Mike then reported the details of the arrest of the defendant. The defendant, Chai Wanlin, stated that he came to Shanghai in 1918 but often traveled between Harbin and Vladivostok. The firearm was deposited by a friend who had gone to Hong Kong. He did not know the plaintiff. He claimed that he was drunk on the day in question and that the plaintiff's car was behind his car and that the bright lights had blinded him, causing him to become angry. He then argued with the plaintiff's driver and took out his gun to threaten him, but he did not fire it. When asked in court why he was carrying a weapon, he claimed that because the Hongqiao area was remote, he had encountered thieves there two years ago and carried a weapon for self-defense. Chai's driver, Yishanke, stated that he was repairing the car tire at the time and did not notice whether the master had fired the gun, but he did hear a gunshot. The court ordered the two Russians to be remanded in custody and rescheduled the hearing for August 13 to summon all the witnesses for further questioning.

Trial of Kidnapping Cousin Case 168

Yang Zhaoxian, from Jiangbei, who did not engage in honest work, colluded with Chen Huanwen, Jiang Wenxuan, and his concubine Yang Wangshi to kidnap the four-year-old son of his aunt Wu Zhang, who lived in Yinghua Lane, Roberts Road, and hid him in a shed at No. 12 Zhoujia Bridge. The kidnapping occurred on the 27th day of the lunar calendar, and the child was found by detectives on the 28th. Because the shed was originally an empty house, but three mats were found during the search, proving that the accomplices had slept there, Yang Zhaoxian, Chen Huanwen, Jiang Wenxuan, and Yang Wangshi were transferred to the District Court, where the prosecutor investigated and filed a public prosecution for kidnapping. Yesterday morning, Judge Qian Chengjun opened the trial. According to Yang Zhaoxian's confession, the child was his cousin, and he had taken him to play, colluding with Chen Huanwen and others to take him. Jiang Wenxuan was responsible for finding the house. Chen Huanwen also confessed that he was brought along by Yang Zhaoxian, and Yang Wangshi was responsible for guarding the child later. Jiang Wenxuan also confessed that he was a rickshaw puller and had rented the house after being led there. Yang Wangshi confessed that after her husband died, she became the concubine of Yang Guangxian. This time, she was guarding the child on Yang Zhaoxian's instructions, but she was very afraid of him and dared not disobey him. The judge noted that the four plaintiffs in the case had not arrived, so the debate was not opened, and the defendants were all remanded in custody for further summons.

Typesetter for Western Newspaper Attacked by Enemies 169

Wang Chengfa, a 23-year-old Suzhou native who worked as a typesetter for the local "Continental Daily," was walking in Taiyuan Lane, French Concession, at 10:40 p.m. last night when he was suddenly attacked by three or four enemies. Without asking any questions, they pulled out sharp knives and slashed at him, inflicting one knife wound on his left leg, five knife wounds on his back, and one knife wound on his neck. Blood flowed like a river. By the time the police from Post No. 445 arrived, the murderers had fled without a trace. The police transported him to Renji Hospital for treatment.

He Si Abducts a Married Woman 170

Su Jishi, a 31-year-old woman from Hai'an, and her husband, Mr. Su, were farmers in their hometown. Because Mr. Su felt that farming was laborious and the production was limited, he came to Shanghai to pull a rickshaw. After arriving in Shanghai, he made a good income every day, so he stayed in Shanghai and did not think about returning home. His wife, Ms. Ji, waited at home for too long and became anxious. She accompanied her brother, Ji Airong, to Shanghai and stayed at the home of Chen Baosheng, a fellow villager. She then paid attention to finding her husband's whereabouts. A man named He Si, aged 31, who lived at No. 52 Huining Road in the South City, was a rickshaw puller and was acquainted with Chen Baosheng. He often went to Chen's house at No. 43 South Railway Station Branch Road to play. He saw that Su Jishi was attractive and secretly tried to seduce her. Before long, they fell in love and had an affair. On the first of this month, they eloped together. When Ms. Ji and her brother saw that Ms. Ji's husband had disappeared, they searched everywhere without any news. Until yesterday morning at about 8:00 a.m., they happened to meet Ms. Ji near Nanjing Road and saw that He Si was also accompanying her. They immediately stepped forward and grabbed the man and woman and turned them over to the shift patrol police Ma Yuqin of the First District, First Precinct. The precinct chief interrogated them and, considering that the matter involved the abduction of a married woman, ordered that a written report be prepared and sent to the Shanghai District Court for investigation.

Two Divorce Cases 171

Ye Meixian, a young woman from Ningbo, 24 years old, married Chen Zhikui, a fellow villager, at the age of 22. Now, due to differences in opinion, she has hired lawyers Xue Jiaqi and Wang Zuxun to file a lawsuit for divorce with the District Court. The petition states that in the spring of 1930, Chen Ren, a matchmaker, arranged a marriage between the plaintiff and the defendant, Chen Zhikui, with the consent of both parents. The wedding was held on April 22 of that year at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association. However, the defendant was fond of gambling and pawned the plaintiff's clothes. The plaintiff repeatedly advised him to stop, but to no avail. On January 17 of this year, the defendant's father severed his relationship with the defendant, and the plaintiff was repeatedly abused and could not live together. She turned to the Women's Association for relief. After mediation by her old neighbor Wang Wenkui and Ms. Zhu Xingyin of the Women's Association, the defendant voluntarily repented and wrote a letter of repentance, promising to return to good behavior. However, the defendant's bad habits were difficult to eradicate, and the plaintiff was still abused. The plaintiff's three-year-old son was taken away and hidden by the defendant. Such a situation is truly a break in affection and unbearable to live with. According to the precedents of the former Supreme Court (5th Year, Shang Zi No. 1073, 7th Year, Shang Zi No. 150), it constitutes grounds for divorce. Therefore, the plaintiff requests that the divorce be granted. Furthermore, the son of the plaintiff and defendant is only three years old and should not be separated from his mother. The plaintiff requests that the defendant be ordered to hand over the custody of the child to the plaintiff and that the alimony to be paid should be reserved for a separate lawsuit.

The defendant, Chen Zhikui, also hired lawyers Huang Han and Gu Jirong to defend and file a counterclaim requesting cohabitation. He stated that since the defendant and plaintiff married, their relationship has been good, and they have a three-year-old boy. The defendant previously worked in a foreign firm and resigned due to a minor incident. The plaintiff accused him of gambling, which is all fabricated and slanderous. The defendant's father runs a shop, and the defendant previously had private savings deposited in his father's shop. Later, because the plaintiff and her parents-in-law did not get along, the defendant had to separate from his parents and withdraw the money from the shop, which angered his father. He has now reconciled with his parents. After the defendant separated from his parents, he set up a small family. There were disputes with the plaintiff over trivial household matters, but there was no abuse or insult. Spouses have an obligation to cohabit, which was established by the former Supreme Court's precedents. Therefore, the plaintiff requests that the plaintiff's lawsuit be rejected and that cohabitation be ordered. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang Qufei specially opened the Second Tribunal to hear the case. Both parties arrived with their lawyers. According to the plaintiff Ye Meixian's testimony, she recounted the previous events and requested that the divorce be granted. The defendant, Chen Zhikui, stated that he was 25 years old, lived at No. 7 Kongjia Lane in Ximennei, and was currently engaged in exchange business. He and his wife had always been harmonious and did not want a divorce. He requested cohabitation. The judge then invited Prosecutor Lei Renlong to express his opinion and had the lawyers hired by both parties to debate with each other. The judge considered the debate to be concluded and scheduled the judgment for August 8.

Liu Chengrui, a young woman from Suqian, Jiangsu, currently residing at No. 35, Lane 4, Southwest Lane, Shanghai-Minhang South Extension Road, has hired lawyer Hu Yuanjun to file a lawsuit with the District Court, alleging that her husband, Sun Changyun, is addicted to bad habits, disregards her support, and arbitrarily insults and abuses her. She requests a divorce and that a public notice be served. Yesterday morning, Judge Wang opened the trial. The defendant did not appear because his address was unknown and he could not be served. A special agent, lawyer Zhou Yu, appeared to defend him. The plaintiff, Liu Chengrui, stated that she was 25 years old and that her husband, Sun Changyun, was 29 years old, also from Suqian. She married him when she was 19 years old and has not lived with him for two years. Her husband worked for a living and earned more than ten yuan a month. The judge asked, "Do you have evidence that the defendant abused you?" She replied, "No, but it is true that he beat me. Last year, I was beaten all over." The judge asked, "Since he beat you, you should have reported it to the police." She replied, "I did not report it." Prosecutor Zhao then rose to express his opinion, stating that the plaintiff claimed that she was beaten and injured by the defendant, but the plaintiff did not go to the prosecutor's office for examination, so there is no way to prove it. He should investigate the matter further and render a judgment in accordance with the law. The plaintiff's lawyer and the special agent lawyer then debated with each other. The judge ordered that witnesses be summoned for further hearing and verification.

Miserable Death of a Female Worker Working While Ill 172

The Factory Provides Coffin and Burial Expenses

At 8:40 a.m. the day before yesterday, the Huishan Police Station received a report from Shi Xiaozhong, the secretary of the Dahua Cloth Factory at No. 150 Elcock Road, stating that a female worker, Xiang Tao, had died at the factory gate. The police sent detectives to investigate and found that Ms. Xiang was only 21 years old and had been working in the factory. She had been suffering from diarrhea for more than ten days, but due to financial difficulties, she continued to work at the factory while ill. She died due to illness. The body was then transported to the morgue. Yesterday morning, Xu Mei, a prosecutor appointed by the Special District Court, arrived at the morgue to examine the body. After examining the body, he questioned the deceased's husband, Xiang Sanmei. Xiang stated that he worked as a tea boy in the Huizhong Hotel and earned very little money. He requested that the factory provide compensation. Shi Xiaozhong stated that there was no such rule in the factory unless the employees contributed one or two yuan for funeral expenses. Xu then ordered that the deceased, Xiang Tao, had died of illness. The deceased's family was struggling and could not afford a coffin. The Dahua Cloth Factory should provide twenty yuan for burial expenses, and the body should be handed over to the deceased's husband for burial.

Fire in Tangshan Road 173

Six People Injured Jumping from Buildings to Escape

A fire suddenly broke out in Donggui Lane, Tangshan Road, last night at 11:00 p.m., spreading to as many as six buildings. Residents inside the buildings, seeing the raging fire, rushed to escape. Many jumped from the windows, and six people were injured from the falls. All were carried to Renji Hospital for treatment by firefighters. Two of them were seriously injured and their lives were in danger. The fire was extinguished at 2:00 a.m. this morning.

Unidentified Floating Body in Huangpu River 174

How the Death Occurred Has Not Yet Been Determined

An unidentified male body suddenly floated to the surface of the Huangpu River at the dock of the Dongyang Company in Hongkou at about 9:00 a.m. yesterday. The body was wearing a white cloth shirt and trousers, black socks, and black leather shoes, and was about 20 years old. It is still difficult to determine whether the death was due to suicide or accidental fall. After being discovered by Chinese police officer No. 42 of the Water Patrol Police, the body was fished out and sent to the South City Rescue Bureau for storage.

A Cursing Incident Leads to a Fatality 175

For the Sake of "Three Pockmarks"

A Life Was Lost

Jin Yuzeng, a native of Haimen, lived in the Riyue Bridge area and had a son named Kouxiang, who was six years old. Last Saturday, a fellow villager named Wang Laosan, who had many pockmarks on his face, was cutting vegetables in the field. Kouxiang, who was naturally naughty, kicked the vegetables over, and Wang scolded him. The child cursed Wang, calling him "Three Pockmarks." Wang Laosan did not mind because he was, in fact, pockmarked. Unexpectedly, Wang's nephew, Zhou Dalang, suddenly became furious and said, "Is the name 'Three Pockmarks' something a snot-nosed kid like you can call?" He wanted to hit the child, but Jin's wife, Wu, seeing that her son was about to be beaten, stopped him and scolded the adult for hitting a child, which was inappropriate. Zhou Dalang became even angrier and clashed with her. Jin also came out to help his wife. Zhou then gathered Mao Xuewen, Shen Baoqing, and others and went to beat Jin severely. Jin was outnumbered and fled outside, thinking of asking his cousin in the North City to come and mediate like Lu Zhonglian. Therefore, he did not return on Saturday, and his wife also fled from home, leaving only their son alone. When he returned home the next day, his son Kouxiang had fallen into the river and drowned. Although Jin found that his son had fallen into the river himself, he believed that the cause of the tragedy was that Zhou Dalang had stirred up trouble for no reason, causing his wife and him to flee and leave their son unattended. Because he could not find Zhou, he brought Mao and Shen to the Second District Police Station. Yesterday, they were brought to the District Court for questioning.

Qiu Junting's Rice Boat Robbed 176

Qiu Junting, a rice boat owner, recently loaded 180 stones of white rice from Wujiang to Shanghai and entrusted it to a rice broker for sale. The day before yesterday afternoon, the boat was sailing in the South Huangpu Taka area. The weather was dark, so they anchored there for the night. Unexpectedly, at midnight, three small boats arrived, carrying more than ten bandits armed with weapons. They swarmed onto the boat and forced their way into the cabin. Qiu and the six crew members woke up in surprise and, seeing that they were bandits, resisted them. However, the bandits outnumbered them, and two crew members were severely injured by the bandits' knives and sticks. Qiu's head was also injured. The bandits drove the people on the boat to the bow and monitored them. One of the crew members took advantage of the bandits' inattention and jumped ashore, blowing a police whistle. The villagers in the area heard the sound and came out to investigate. After being informed by the crew, they rushed to help. At that time, the bandits were opening the hold to loot the rice. Seeing the villagers gathering, they jumped onto the three small boats and fled south. Two anti-smuggling patrol boats passed by and, after being informed by Qiu, chased after them. Qiu checked and found that a small leather box had been robbed, containing seventy or eighty yuan in foreign currency for paying taxes and two letters entrusted by inlanders, containing drafts. Fortunately, the rice was not robbed. Two crew members were taken to the hospital after arriving in Minhang yesterday. Qiu was not seriously injured and was discharged from the hospital on the spot. The two crew members were seriously injured and remained in the hospital for treatment. In the afternoon, Qiu took a car to Shanghai to report to the rice broker and borrow money to return and open the boat to Shanghai to pay the taxes at the tax card. Upon learning of the incident, the rice boat owners in Shanghai were all on alert and dared not travel alone.

Three Thieves Arrested in Baierbu Road 177

A Chinese detective of the Public Concession Huishi Police Station received a tip that several thieves who had repeatedly committed theft cases in the concession were hiding in the pavilion of No. 7 Chengli, Baierbu Road, French Concession. Therefore, at about 5:00 a.m. yesterday morning, many Chinese and Western detectives, along with informants, first went to the French police station to ask for assistance in making the arrest. They then went to the address and arrested three people in the house, bringing them all to the police station to await interrogation.

The Tragedy of the Sand Dredger Collision 178

The Boat Owner Suffered Heavy Injuries

The Crew Member Drowned on the Spot

The Shaoxing reed mat boat, "Qian Shunxing," loaded with sand and mud for sale in Shanghai, arrived at Zhanghuabang Bay in Songnan around 3 a.m. the day before yesterday, before dawn. It happened to encounter the Ningxing steamship of the Sanbei Company sailing out. Unable to avoid the collision, the sand dredger's mast was broken, and the hull was damaged. The boat owner, Qian A'ang, was working on the deck and was struck. His right ear was severely lacerated, and his right arm was seriously injured. All five crew members fell into the water. Subsequently, a certain fishing boat came to the rescue and saved four of them, but crew member Chen Rongxiang drowned before he could be rescued. After the accident, the crew managed to sail the boat to Wusong and beach it on a sandbar. The injured boat owner was immediately sent to Wusong Hospital for treatment. After reporting the incident to Jiang Gongxing, the owner of the tax reporting firm, Jiang Wenxing, rushed to Shanghai to negotiate with the Sanbei Company. The company agreed to investigate the circumstances and discuss a peaceful resolution. Therefore, the boat owner has not yet submitted a report to the Water Police Station or the Customs River Port Department for assistance.

The Madman on the Muddy Ferry Street 179

Yesterday morning at 1 a.m., a man wandered back and forth on Muddy Ferry Street in Pudong, waving his hands and feet, muttering incoherently, appearing insane. The police on duty attempted to drive him away, but he became agitated and irrational. They immediately detained him at the Third District Public Security Bureau to inquire about his name, age, and address. The man spoke incoherently, seemingly mentally disturbed. After his mind cleared slightly, he identified himself as Li Laigen, 44 years old, from Chongming. His other statements were vague, and he did not provide a clear address. The District Chief instructed that he be sent to the main bureau for further action.

Suspect Arrested in Tobacco Leaf Theft Case 180

Regarding the case of the Hua Fang Transportation Company having its tobacco leaves stolen by wharf bandits on the 29th of last month, a report was filed with the Water Police Station, which dispatched detectives to investigate and apprehend the suspects. Yesterday, Huatans Sun A'gui and Wang Haiquan of the police station discovered that the bandits were hiding in Qichangzhan, Pudong. They reported to the Third District Public Security Bureau's branch office, where Patrol Chief Shen led police officers to assist in the arrest. Eight suspects were apprehended, including Zhang Gui, Huang Liansheng, Cao Jinghua, Yang San, Huang A'san, Li Huihai, Wang Kelin, and Wen Lizhao, all from Tongzhou. They were sent to the Third District Headquarters, where District Chief Zhang questioned them before handing them back to the original detectives for further investigation.

Wang Yucheng Resolutely Resigns from Hometown Association Post 181

The Anhui Native Place Association in Shanghai has formally taken office after the recent re-election of committee members. Wang Yucheng, an executive committee member, citing advanced age and declining strength, felt unable to perform his duties effectively. In addition to firmly resigning from the association, he had already published a notice of resignation in the newspaper to show his determination. Recently, upon receiving the association's letter of appointment, Mr. Wang returned the original letter to the association.

French Concession

Another Gambling Den Telephone Uncovered 182

Shi A'sheng Fined Fifty Dollars

Shi A'sheng recently set up a gambling den with a telephone in the French Concession, enticing people to gamble in violation of the law. The French police detectives discovered this and raided the premises, seizing gambling documents and silver dollars. Yesterday, he was brought to the French court for trial. The police chief reported the situation, and Shi confessed to setting up a gambling den with a telephone to entice gambling. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced him to a fine of fifty dollars to be confiscated as a warning.

Electrician Electrocuted to Death 183

Yang Qingfu, a 21-year-old electrical technician at the Dakang Yarn Factory in Yangshupu, was repairing a machine yesterday afternoon when he accidentally touched an electrical wire. He immediately lost consciousness and was rushed to Tongren Hospital, but it was too late, and he died. His body was sent to the coroner's office for an autopsy.

Prohibition of Zhongyuan Rituals 184

Originally to Prevent Gangsters from Extorting Money

Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau Director Yuan recently issued an order, noting that with the arrival of autumn, local gangsters often use the excuse of holding Menglan Sheng Hui (Ghost Festival) to extort money. Now that superstition is being eliminated, strict measures should be taken. Director Yuan specifically instructed all district offices that if any local thugs are found using the excuse of the Zhongyuan Festival to solicit donations from door to door and hire monks and Taoists to perform rituals, they should be immediately detained and investigated to eliminate superstition.

The American Palm Olive Company has had a branch in China for ten years, with Mr. Ma Bole serving as the Chinese manager. His plans and policies are deeply in line with the psychology of both Chinese and American people, which has led to such rapid business development. Yesterday, Western goods industry colleagues held a public banquet for Mr. Ma at the Ye Family Garden in Jiangwan to celebrate his departure for the United States on the 29th of this month. The scene was bustling and lively, and a photograph was taken to commemorate the occasion. It is said that Mr. Ma's trip is at the invitation of the American headquarters to inspect various factories in the United States for about half a year. Upon his return, the company will surely undergo further development, not only benefiting Sino-American trade but also strengthening friendly relations.

(5) The matter of the Central University Medical School sending Chinese representative Peiss to attend the International Medical Conference concerns the dignity of Chinese scholars. It was resolved that the association should send a letter of warning to the Central University Medical School, urging it to consider the overall national interest, promote academics, and reassign a Chinese scholar. If re-election is not possible, it is better to abstain from attending. If a non-first-class medical expert foreigner is sent as a representative, the association will send a telegram to the International Commercial Association to deny it. The above intentions were handed over to the document committee to draft a letter and proceed immediately. (6) The publication date of the Medical Journal should be specified. It was resolved that, starting with the second issue, the volume designation should be cancelled and four issues should be published each year in February, May, August, and November. Any delayed issues should be made up immediately. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Lost Unnamed Girl Waiting to be Claimed 192

The Municipal Public Security Bureau sent a lost unnamed girl from the Third Precinct of the Fourth District yesterday. The girl was found lost in Zhengjiazhai Township, Zhenru, on August 1st at 11:00 AM. She is about five or six years old and has two small braids tied with red velvet rope on the back of her head. She wears a silver earring on her right ear and a black thread on her left ear. She wears a silver necklace and white five-color material bracelets on both hands. Female Abductor Sentenced to One Year Imprisonment 193

The abductor, Ding Daishi, abducted girls Chen Jinqiao and boy Cai Bao, etc., on a Zhejiang steamer, planning to go to Xiamen to sell them. She hid the children in a quilt, thinking she could escape the eyes of the detectives. However, before the ship had set sail, the relief society investigators Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang boarded the ship to check for abduction. Upon reaching Ms. Ding's place, they saw a bulge in the bedding and became suspicious. Opening the quilt revealed the truth. Several pills were also found, suspected to be narcotics. Ms. Ding was taken to the local court. After the prosecutor's investigation and examination of the pills, it was found that they contained opium for addiction and were not narcotics. The prosecutor filed a public lawsuit citing the abduction and opium crimes. After the trial, the debate concluded, and yesterday, Ding Daishi was sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined 60 yuan. She was ordered to be returned to prison for execution of the sentence.

Local News Two

Two Pieces of Human Flesh in Paper Packages 202

A Portion of the Tragically Deceased Female Corpse

Discovered Beside the Public Latrine

Two alarming paper packages were found by the public latrine on Shandong Road, north of Hankou Road, yesterday morning. Upon opening them, they were found to contain human flesh, cut from a dismembered female corpse, causing a stir among onlookers. The flesh had been rotting for some time, emitting a foul odor that was nauseating, and the flesh was covered in knife marks, causing the viewers to shudder. The origin of these two pieces of corpse flesh remains a mystery.

Discovery of Paper Packages 203

Yesterday morning, a public latrine worker named 32nd saw two paper packages placed beside the wall while working at the Shandong Road public latrine. The packages were neatly wrapped, as if they had been forgotten by someone relieving themselves. The worker watched and waited for a long time, but no one came to retrieve them, so he began to suspect something. Two police officers from number 2304 happened to pass by, and the worker reported the matter. They could not guess what was inside the packages, so they cautiously opened them and were horrified.

Horrifying Human Flesh 204

The two packages were roughly rectangular in shape and tightly wrapped. After successively removing the outer wrapping of newspaper and kraft paper, a foul odor struck the nose and became unbearable. When the paper packages were opened, what came into view was human flesh from a female corpse. One piece seemed to be the chest, with the shoulders, neck, and upper limbs removed. The other piece was slightly connected to the thigh muscles and was badly decomposed. In addition to the numerous knife marks, there was also a scorched color, as if it had been burned.

Conflicting Opinions 205

The Central Police Station was informed of the matter and immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to investigate. There is no doubt that this case involves murder and the disposal of a corpse, but the origin of the corpse and the identity of the murderer remain a mystery. Nearby residents were quite excited about this matter, and there were conflicting rumors. One said that the corpse had been placed in the public latrine the night before, and that the person who placed it there was a rickshaw puller.

A Glimmer of Hope 206

It is said that the day before yesterday evening, a rickshaw puller surnamed Jia came from the North Station pulling a rickshaw southward. The passenger was carrying two paper packages and seemed quite concerned about them. When the rickshaw reached the Qinglian Pavilion near Fuzhou Road, the passenger suddenly made an excuse to get out of the rickshaw and left, never to return. The rickshaw puller then disappeared as well. If this is true, it is a glimmer of hope and is recorded here.

A Car Stopped Beside La Du Road

Thugs Whispering Secretly 207

A Bodyguard of a Residence Grew Suspicious

A Large Number of Detectives Rushed to Investigate

Both Sides Opened Fire but Neither Hit

Two People Were Arrested and Three Escaped

At 4:45 p.m. yesterday, several thugs suddenly appeared near the intersection of Lafayette Road and La Du Road in the French Concession, loitering at the corner of the road with malicious intent. Fortunately, a residence was nearby, and the bodyguard noticed them and secretly reported to the police by telephone. Chinese and Western detectives rushed to the scene to apprehend them. Two people were arrested on the spot, and both sides fired a shot, but neither hit. The details are recorded below.

Whispering Secretly by the Roadside 208

At around 4 p.m. yesterday, a white-licensed car number 12418 suddenly appeared near the intersection of Lafayette Road and La Du Road in the French Concession and stopped at the corner of the road. Two people were sitting in the car, wearing dark blue silk shirts. After the car stopped, one person hurried out of the car and whispered secretly with three people who were already standing on the grass there. Their expressions were unusually secretive.

The Bodyguard Became Suspicious 209

The group stood and whispered for a long time, looking around as if waiting for something. A few bodyguards of a residence were standing on the opposite side of the grass, watching from the entrance. Suddenly, they caught sight of several people gathering across the street, and a car was parked by the roadside. Suspicion arose.

Detectives Rushed to the Scene by Car 210

The bodyguards carefully observed the clothing of the people, and at times glanced across the street. After a quarter of an hour, the bodyguards concluded that the people were not good. They immediately turned around, entered the house, and reported to the police by telephone. Upon hearing the news, the police chief ordered Western detective Yang Guosi, Chinese deputy detective chief Mao Jingen, Bao detective Qin Youyu, Zhou Bugeng, etc. from the theft case squad to rush to the scene by car.

Western Detective Waved Frequently 211

When the detectives arrived at the destination, they saw a white-licensed car number 12418 parked by the roadside. Two people wearing black Indian silk long shirts were standing beside the car. About forty yards away from the left side of the car, three people wearing linen long shirts and short clothes were also standing on the grass. Their behavior was suspicious. The detectives immediately approached the car, first checking the two people standing beside the car and the driver. Then, Western detective Yang Guosi waved to the three people on the grass.

Both Sides Fired a Shot 212

When the detectives checked the car, the three people standing on the grass remained still, their attitudes unusually calm. When the Western detective waved to them, one of them suddenly pulled out a pistol and fired a shot at the detectives, while fleeing southward. Western detective Yang also drew his gun and returned fire, but just as he fired a shot, the second bullet was suddenly jammed in the breech, so neither side was hit.

Two People Were Arrested and Interrogated 213

After the thugs opened fire, they immediately fled into the Chinese territory and could not be found. The detectives immediately took the two people standing beside the car, along with the car and the driver, into the police station for questioning. One person identified himself as Wang A'gen, from Jiangbei, and said he was the leader of the picket squad in a certain labor union's strike committee. The other person, Su Jianliang, a local, said he was a member of the picket squad. The remaining statements were evasive.

The Driver's Statement Was Consistent 214

After questioning the driver, who identified himself as Chen Yinhuan, from Changzhou, and said he was a driver at the Dongxin Automobile Company, Bao Yu Lane, 299-301 Edward Road, he said that at around 3:50 p.m. today (yesterday), two people wearing black silk long shirts suddenly came to the company to hire a car, stating that they would be dropped off at Lujiawan. He (the driver) drove the number 12418 car there, but they did not go directly to Lujiawan, instead going to the intersection of Lafayette Road and La Du Road and parking there for about a quarter of an hour before being arrested by the Bao detective, etc. The police chief, according to the statement, immediately ordered the owner of the car company to bail out the two arrested men and await trial in court.

Flourishing Market in Western Shanghai 215

Eighty or Ninety Percent Located in Chinese Territory

The Overreach of the Shanghai Municipal Council is Frightening

Chinese People Should Urgently Pay Attention

The prosperity of the entire city of Shanghai is increasing daily. Considering just the area of Western Shanghai, which we frequent daily, the emergence of new buildings is already astonishing. For example, on Connaught Road, five years ago, the entire road was mostly vacant land. Now, magnificent buildings line both sides. The section of Medhurst Road to Gordon Road is experiencing booming business, almost becoming a second New Zhapu Road. The section of Xiaoshadu Road around Jiangjia Bridge, as well as the dog racing track, also have continuous shops and markets being established. The public bus company is particularly thriving to Jessfield Road, with the entire road having many exquisite Chinese and Western high-class residences, with toilets, electricity, and running water fully equipped. In the early morning and as the sun sets, pedestrians are like weaving cloth. The original flourishing section of Robison Road was only around Yinhua Lane. Now, shops are densely packed along the entire road. Except for factories, the buildings are slightly inferior to those on Connaught Road. The section of Jessfield Road from Jing'an Temple to Wujiaochang, such as Yuanshan Lane and Xinkang Lane, and the high-end Chinese-style residences and shops currently under construction for rent, will number over a thousand. The vacant land of the Shanghai Municipal Council in Wujiaochang and the old houses on all sides have been renovated. The prosperity of Wujiaochang is like that of North Nicheng Bridge ten years ago, and the new buildings there still seek to exceed supply. The bustling scene at Daba, where the land has already been fully leased, is evident from this. Haig Road, Edinburgh Road, and Yuyuan Road, etc., are already recognized as the best locations for large residences, with towering trees, dense shade, and continuous rows of grand buildings. Great Western Road and Hongqiao Road, etc., have already become the tail end of the new residential area. The new buildings in the Xujiahui Beidang Road Nanyang University area are also quite numerous, particularly high-end and exquisite. In the near future, the progress of prosperity in Western Shanghai has truly unlimited potential. Eighty or ninety percent of the above is located in Chinese territory, while the overreach of the Shanghai Municipal Council in building roads is unrestrained. No wonder the aggressive ambitions of the Shanghai Municipal Council are also rising with the booming local economy. Therefore, I present this to bring it to the attention of the Chinese people.

The Truth Behind Hao Futian's Suicide 216

Terrible Circumstances

Tragic Suicide Note

This newspaper previously reported on the young man and woman, a Mr. Hao and Ms. Fu Yu, who committed suicide together in Wusong. Friends and relatives of both parties received news on the day of their suicide and successively retrieved their bodies from the scene of the incident. Mr. Hao's friends and relatives knew that his father was over sixty years old and quick-tempered. He was currently residing with relatives of the Shen family in Sihe Lane in the French Concession. They were deeply afraid that once he heard this news, something unexpected might happen. In addition to arranging the funeral, they also sent a telegram urging his younger brother, Hao Gengsheng, to come to Shanghai quickly to comfort his elderly father. Therefore, they strictly kept the cause of Hao's death a secret in order to hide it from his father. Unexpectedly, he suspected the report in the newspaper and paid close attention to the investigation. Once he discovered the secret, he

Burst into Inconsolable Cries 217

And was overwhelmed with grief. Friends and relatives then tried to comfort him and sent someone from the Shen residence to watch over him to prevent any accidents. Mr. Hao's name was Futian, 36 years old, and he was a brilliant student from Huai'an People's Middle School, excelling in both Chinese and Western languages. Ren Jinping, Sun Daosheng, Tao Xiaofang, Gu Kenfu, and others were all his close classmates. After leaving school, he was hired by the local Minsheng Girls' School

As Head of Academics 218

And was extremely enthusiastic about school affairs. During the European War, he strongly supported Duan Qirui's advocacy of participating in the war and then enlisted as a translator for Chinese laborers, going to France with the Chinese labor corps. Before leaving, he entrusted Ren Jinping to act as his head of academics and also entrusted the three gentlemen Sun, Tao, and Gu to assist together, and further used the

Bullets and Rain of Shells 219

The salary he received under those conditions, allocating one-tenth of it to be sent monthly to Hong Kong to support Minsheng Girls' School. Mr. Hao made real and powerful contributions to Minsheng's ability to achieve its current success. While in France, he befriended Mr. Xia Qifeng, former secretary of the League of Nations. At that time, Mr. Xia led the majority of translators in fighting for the right of hundreds of thousands of Chinese laborers to participate in the war, and Mr. Hao also greatly supported this. When he returned to China, because of his

Suicide Note 225

Brother, I am now dead. Before dying, I originally had plans to run away, but the terrible circumstances did not allow for any leniency, inevitably forcing me to die. This is truly a helpless matter. Younger brother, you are my confidant, so close that we are like flesh and blood. Therefore, although I did not want others to know of my death, I cannot but say this first. I only hope that this matter will not be made public to others, and that you will understand my suffering and not blame me. I have a friend who, because he could not maintain his business, which had already closed down, wanted to raise 500 yuan to settle debts and rebuild his business. However, in a period of one month, expending nine years and two tigers' worth of effort, he only obtained 150 yuan. Because the funds obtained were of no use, he had a desire for luck and sought to make a desperate gamble. He came to ask me to go with him. I was especially foolish and went with him. Unexpectedly, this sum of money obtained with great difficulty was completely taken by the casino's income in the blink of an eye. After the friend suffered this setback, his mind was not right and he wanted to commit suicide. I then tried to stop him and ran to Wang Erdao's house to borrow the remaining 50 yuan in tuition fees. I went to the casino again, hoping to try my luck, but unfortunately, I still lost. My friend's desire to commit suicide then became even more determined. Although there had been discussions about running away, in the end, there was no way to go and there was only one death. Because I could not save my friend's death, nor could I disregard my friend's death. Moreover, after my friend's death, I, who jointly created this cause of death, was still living alone. Not only did I have no face to see my friend's family and the friends who knew us both, but I also had no way to comfort my conscience. In the deep of the night, I felt that, apart from my parents, there was nothing that could make me stay. My former ambition had long since dissipated, so the result that no one can escape, I advanced the deadline to shorten the pain of economic oppression, which may not have been an unpleasant thing. Calculating that when this letter reaches you, brother and my friend will have both followed Poseidon on a journey to paradise. After you receive this letter, you will definitely deeply blame me for not telling you, but I know that your plight is no different from mine, and your responsibility is heavy, and the amount of your debt is dozens of times greater than mine. Although 150 yuan could be raised with effort, I could not bear to add to my brother's burden with this improper failure. Moreover, even if I got 150 yuan, it could only relieve my responsibility and may not be able to save my friend's death. Rather than seeing my friend die and living, it is better to stay away from the evil environment and die. I am now dead. With the evil forces of the environment, I will not be able to help you in the future. Brother, you should congratulate me and never be sad for me. Brother, you have extraordinary talent and extraordinary perseverance. You have been fighting against the evil environment for four or five years, and this evil environment has never been able to do anything to you, so the final victory must be near at hand. I hope that you will continue your usual advocacy and forge ahead bravely, so that I can see the environment that killed me and be overcome by my brother in the afterlife. If the soul is conscious, it must be happy. The future is great, I hope you will take care of yourself and pray for you to comfort our elderly father from time to time, so that he will not be too sad. Crying out at the moment of death is the ultimate trust. The place where we die is outside the mouth of Wusong, and the bodies will soon go away with the waves, so there is no need to search for them meaninglessly. Sea burial is better than land burial, which occupies land. Brother knows, Le Li

I have unnecessary worries, you advised me to relax on the Shanghai beach, I am willing enough, you now suddenly die, I hesitate to deal with the aftermath for you, is your heart at peace?

A Romanian Man

Opens a Roulette Gambling Den 227

Müller Fined Three Thousand Yuan

Gambling Patrons Hired are Fined Separately

A Romanian man named Müller recently set up a private roulette gambling den in a Western-style house at No. 47 Rue Massenet in the French Concession, hiring ten Chinese people, Ji Ruiqing, Zhong Bohua, Wang Yongfu, Long Er, Zhu Bingsheng, Wang Xueshan, Bian Shuanggui, Xu Ajin, Chen Zhonglin, and Qiu Gensheng, to serve as hosts and other positions inside. Afterwards, Western Detective of the French Police Department, after learning of the situation, led detectives Xu Fuqing, Li Liansheng, and others to raid the location the night before, seizing two sets of roulette gambling equipment, more than 1,000 yuan in cash, and taking the owner, employees, and gamblers to the police station. After questioning them, the police chief ordered Müller and others to post bail, lightly fined the gamblers, and dismissed them. Yesterday, they were taken to the French court for further investigation. First, the Western detective reported the previous situation and presented the gambling equipment and silver dollars as evidence. When questioned, Müller confessed to running a private gambling operation. When questioned, Ji Ruiqing and others confessed to being hired by Müller to work inside as civilians, and the remaining confessions were evasive. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Müller to a fine of 3,000 yuan, Ji Ruiqing, Zhong Bohua, and Wang Yongfu to a fine of 200 yuan each, and the rest to a fine of 50 yuan each, all to be confiscated. The seized gambling equipment and silver dollars were also confiscated. The former Yueyu Lane

Prostitute Mei Fei is Accused 228

Zhao Guangzuo is Infatuated with Mei Fei

His Wife Files a Criminal Complaint

Mei Fei, formerly a prostitute in Yueyu Lane on Guangxi Road, now named Chen Junxia, has recently been criminally charged in the Special District Court by Zhao Tan Meiying, the wife of local resident Zhao Guangzuo, for embezzlement of an ownership certificate for a car with the intent to defraud. She claims that since her husband, Zhao Guangzuo, began visiting the defendant, the defendant has enticed him, preventing him from returning home day and night. In less than half a year, he has spent over ten thousand yuan. This spring, relatives, seeing that Guangzuo was young and easily led astray, strongly advocated for marrying the plaintiff in order to persuade him. Unexpectedly, on the night of the wedding, Guangzuo was summoned by the defendant, and his small savings were transferred overnight. Until the end of June this year, the defendant incited Guangzuo to buy a new car, causing him to take the family's ancestral ownership certificate and mortgage it outside for her own free use. Guangzuo is surrounded by the defendant's charms, indulging himself all day long, with his mind confused and his judgment lost. She even dares to instigate Guangzuo to send a letter to the plaintiff, demanding a divorce in order to achieve her cunning plan to break up the family. If this is not punished, how can law, reason, and human sentiment be maintained? She demands legal punishment, etc. It is reported that the court has already summoned them for questioning.

Two British Deserters Captured 229

Yesterday at around 11:00 AM, two foreign soldiers, wearing incomplete uniforms, suddenly came rushing along the riverside of Caojiadu Creek in Western Shanghai, appearing extremely flustered and panicked. Coincidentally, a Jiangbei sampan was parked on the shore nearby. The two soldiers immediately jumped aboard, determined to raise the anchor and set sail, as if trying to escape. Liu Yongsheng, a patrol officer stationed at the Yongyu Yarn Factory in Beihang, dispatched by the Sixth District Police Station of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, saw this and immediately stepped forward to capture the two foreign soldiers and take them back to the district. District Chief Ren questioned them, and the two soldiers confessed that one was named Taolun (transliteration) and the other was named Lintie (transliteration), both of British nationality, serving as soldiers in the British barracks at the Zhaofeng Garden on Jessfield Road. Currently, they were being confined in the barracks for committing offenses, so they took the opportunity to escape, intending to go elsewhere, etc. After obtaining their confessions, District Chief Ren, considering that the two British soldiers were escapees who had committed offenses, should be handed over to the relevant authorities for questioning and punishment in accordance with international practice. In addition to immediately reporting the case to the Municipal Public Security Bureau by telephone for record-keeping, he also notified the head of the Jing'an Temple Police Station to dispatch Deputy Police Officer No. 208 to take the two British deserters back to the police station for verification.

Outside the Mouth of Wusong

The Dingxing and Ruifeng Sands are Robbed 230

Wang Buyun, the head of Dingxing Sand Duck Nest Sand (i.e., Shitou Sand) outside the mouth of Wusong, his son, and five farmers including Shi Shangzhi, were previously kidnapped by Chen Guoliang, Wang Youcai, Zhang Jinliu, and other water police squad leaders from the 17th squad of the Wusong Fourth District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police Team stationed near Ruifeng Sand, who colluded with bandits. After the people's corps of the two sands and others suspected that Huang Yutang, the patrol officer who supervised the police, and water police Gong Xibao, Wang Luncai, Zhou Chongquan, Peng Jie, and others were involved, they detained Huang and others and sent them to the Baoshan County government for trial. It was repeatedly reported in this newspaper. However, the three escaped policemen, Chen Guoliang, Wang Youcai, and Zhang Jinliu, along with two bandits, once again rode a sailboat to Dingxing Sand around 1:30 PM the day before yesterday to carry out a major robbery. Before leaving, they also twisted the arms of the two sand residents, Gong Daosheng and Tang Fugen, and asked who had ordered them to kidnap Wang Buyun, his son, and others. The people's corps of the two sands sent Patrol Officer Wang and others to the Baoshan County government, asking them to explain quickly who was behind it. Gong and Tang both replied that they really did not know anything about this matter, kneeling on the ground and begging to be released. Chen Guoliang was furious upon hearing that the two were unwilling to tell the truth, and shot Gong Daosheng twice with a handgun, one bullet grazing his neck and the other hitting his left shoulder. At that moment, Gong was injured and fell to the ground. Tang Fugen was ordered by Chen to be stabbed three times in his left arm and thigh with a bayonet by another bandit, also falling to the ground in a pool of blood. Chen then led his gang, carrying the loot, onto the bandit boat and turned to Ruifeng Sand to loot, then sailed towards the open sea and escaped. It is now learned that the residents of these sands are mostly farmers, and most are poor. Therefore, Chen Guoliang and others actually only robbed more than 400 yuan in cash from the two sands, along with clothing and other items, totaling about 1,000 yuan. Because the sands are located in the sea, in addition to a patrol boat dispatched by the Fourth District Water Police stationed there, there are no other security agencies. Therefore, when Chen and others committed the robbery, the general residents all fled and hid in the reeds, allowing them to search and rob at will and leave leisurely. The escaped policemen Chen Guoliang, Wang Youcai, and Zhang Jinfang all used handguns, while the two bandits carried Mauser rifles, but they were all wearing military uniforms, resembling regular troops. After the incident, the people's corps of Dingxing, Ruifeng, and Ping'an Shitou Sands selected representatives to go to the Baoshan County government at around 10:00 AM yesterday to submit a complaint describing the incident and requesting that police be dispatched quickly to protect the area and arrest the bandits. County Chief Qiu, upon receiving the report, immediately consulted with Zhang Han, the district chief of the Fourth District Water Police, requesting that a patrol ship be dispatched for protection. As for the five hostages, Wang Buyun and Shi Shangzhi, the Wang and Shi families have now received letters from the bandits demanding 50,000 yuan for their ransom, with the ransom for Wang Buyun and his son being 20,000 yuan. However, each family cannot raise this huge sum, so they have not yet negotiated with the bandits.
